Therefore, the number of students who suggested adding mashed potatoes is x + 63.
The total number of students who suggested specific types of food is x + (x + 63) = 457.
Combining like terms, we get 2x + 63 = 457.
Subtracting 63 from both sides, we get 2x = 394.
Dividing both sides by 2, we get x = 197.
Therefore, 197 students suggested adding bacon. Answer: \boxed{197}.

Let's say the number of students who suggested adding mashed potatoes is x.
The number of students who suggested adding bacon is x + 166.
The total number of students who suggested adding mashed potatoes and bacon is x + (x + 166) = 182.
This simplifies to 2x + 166 = 182.
Subtracting 166 from both sides gives 2x = 16.
Dividing both sides by 2 gives x = 8.
The number of students who suggested adding bacon is x + 166 = 8 + 166 = <<8+166=174>>174. Answer: \boxed{174}.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is174.

x = $1

14 square feet = 7 feet x Width

Dividing both sides of the equation by 7 feet, we get:

Width = 14 square feet / 7 feet

Width = 2 feet

Therefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet.

229st data
3 red peaches, and some more green peaches are in the basket. If there are 10 more green peaches than red peaches in the basket How many green peaches are in the basket?
Let's assume the number of red peaches in the basket is x.
Therefore, the number of green peaches in the basket is x + 10.
The total number of peaches in the basket is x + (x + 10) = 2x + 10.
Since there are 3 red peaches in the basket, we can write the equation as 2x + 10 = 3.
Subtracting 10 from both sides, we get 2x = 3 - 10 = -7.
Dividing both sides by 2, we get x = -7/2 = -3.5.
Since the number of peaches cannot be negative, we conclude that there are no green peaches in the basket.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is0.

373st data
Together Adam and Jackie have 12 apples. He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do. Adam has 8 more apples than Jackie. How many apples does He have?
Let's assume that Adam has x apples.
Jackie has x + 8 apples.
Together, they have x + (x + 8) = 2x + 8 apples.
He has 9 more apples than Adam and Jackie together, so he has 2x + 8 + 9 = 2x + 17 apples.
Since we know that together they have 12 apples, we can set up the equation 2x + 17 = 12.
Subtracting 17 from both sides, we get 2x = -5.
Dividing both sides by 2, we get x = -2.5.
Since we can't have a negative number of apples, this means that our assumption was incorrect.
Let's try again with a different assumption.
Let's assume that Adam has y apples.
Jackie has y - 8 apples.
Together, they have y + (y - 8) = 2y - 8 apples.
He has 9 more apples than Adam and Jackie together, so he has 2y - 8 + 9 = 2y + 1 apples.
Since we know that together they have 12 apples, we can set up the equation 2y + 1 = 12.
Subtracting 1 from both sides, we get 2y = 11.
Dividing both sides by 2, we get y = 5.5.
Since we can't have a fraction of an apple, this means that our assumption was incorrect.
Therefore, there is no solution to this problem.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) isThere is no solution to this problem.

pred :

Number of weeks in a harvest season = 223 weeks
Number of harvest seasons = 73 harvest seasons

Total earnings = Weekly earnings * Number of weeks in a harvest season * Number of harvest seasons
Total earnings = $1357 * 223 weeks * 73 harvest seasons

Calculating the total earnings:
Total earnings = $1357 * 223 * 73
Total earnings = $26,000,411

Therefore, Lewis will earn $26,000,411 if he works for 73 harvest seasons.

The total number of visitors from the previous day is 419.
The total number of visitors from the day before that is 103.
The total number of visitors from the day Rachel visited is 92.

To find the total number of visitors before that day, we need to subtract the visitors from the previous two days from the total number of visitors.

Total number of visitors before that day = Total number of visitors - Visitors from the previous day - Visitors from the day before that
Total number of visitors before that day = 419 - 103 - 92
Total number of visitors before that day = 224

Therefore, 224 visitors visited the Buckingham palace before the day Rachel visited.

Tiffany was collecting cans for recycling. On monday she had some bags of cans. The next day she found 4 more bags worth of cans. If she had a total of 8 bags altogether How many bags did she have on monday?
Let's say Tiffany had x bags of cans on Monday.
The next day, she found 4 more bags worth of cans, so she had x + 4 bags.
The total number of bags she had altogether is x + (x + 4) = 8 bags.
Combining like terms, we get 2x + 4 = 8.
Subtracting 4 from both sides, we get 2x = 4.
Dividing both sides by 2, we get x = 2.
Therefore, Tiffany had 2 bags of cans on Monday. Answer: \boxed{2}.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is2.

Initially, there were 22 children on the bus.
After 40 children got on the bus, the total number of children on the bus became 22 + 40 = <<22+40=62>>62.
After some children got off the bus, there were 2 children left on the bus.
Therefore, 62 - x = 2.
Simplifying the equation, we get 62 = 2 + x.
Subtracting 2 from both sides, we get 62 - 2 = x.
Thus, x = 60.
Therefore, 60 children got off the bus at the bus stop. Answer: \boxed{60}.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is60.

pred_after : 60
pred : 60

682st data
In a school there are 697 girls and the rest are boys. If there are 228 more girls than boys How many boys are there in that school?
Let's assume the number of boys in the school is x.
According to the given information, the number of girls is 697.
We are also given that there are 228 more girls than boys.
So, the number of girls can be expressed as x + 228.
Since the total number of students in the school is the sum of the number of girls and boys, we can write the equation:
x + (x + 228) = 697
Combining like terms, we get:
2x + 228 = 697
Subtracting 228 from both sides, we get:
2x = 469
Dividing both sides by 2, we get:
x = 234.5
Since the number of boys cannot be a decimal, we round down to the nearest whole number.
Therefore, there are 234 boys in that school. Answer: \boxed{234}.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is234.

Since there are 26 bags with an equal number of cookies, the total number of cookies in all the bags is 26x.

We also know that there are 52 cookies in total, so we can write the equation:

26x = 52

To solve for x, we divide both sides of the equation by 26:

x = 52/26

x = 2

Therefore, each bag has 2 cookies.

Let's assume the distance the frog jumped is x inches.
The grasshopper jumped 4 inches farther than the frog, so the grasshopper jumped x + 4 inches.
The mouse jumped 44 inches lesser than the frog, so the mouse jumped x - 44 inches.
The total distance covered by all three is x + (x + 4) + (x - 44) = 3x - 40 inches.
Given that the grasshopper jumped 19 inches, we have 3x - 40 = 19.
Adding 40 to both sides, we get 3x = 59.
Dividing both sides by 3, we get x = 59/3 = <<59/3=19.666666666666668>>19.67 inches.
Therefore, the frog jumped approximately 19.67 inches. Answer: \boxed{19.67}.

During summer break 800059 kids from Lawrence county go to camp and the rest stay home. Lawrence county has 828521 kids in all. About how many kids stayed home?
To find out how many kids stayed home, we need to subtract the number of kids who went to camp from the total number of kids in Lawrence county.

Number of kids who went to camp = 800059
Total number of kids in Lawrence county = 828521

Number of kids who stayed home = Total number of kids - Number of kids who went to camp
Number of kids who stayed home = 828521 - 800059
Number of kids who stayed home = 28562

Approximately 28,562 kids stayed home.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is28562

There were 6 + 22 = <<6+22=28>>28 roses in the vase before Jessica cut some more.
There were 20 + 21 = <<20+21=41>>41 orchids in the vase before Jessica cut some more.
There are 41 - 21 = <<41-21=20>>20 orchids in the vase now.
There are 22 - 20 = <<22-20=2>>2 more roses than orchids in the vase now. Answer: \boxed{2}.
Therefore, the answer (arabic numerals) is2.

Therefore, Luke scored 22,922 points in the game.

Total number of bird families that flew away = Number of bird families that flew to Africa + Number of bird families that flew to Asia
